- `2026-04-22T10:55:00Z` Follow-up bug fix after the broader post-`MUI-14` hardening pass: the user reported that opening `/opportunities` in the local runtime dropped into the authenticated workspace error boundary. I reproduced that against the live app with a real Chromium session and captured the actual client-side failure: `TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'inputProps')` inside the shared `Select` wrapper when the opportunities filter rail rendered.
- `2026-04-22T10:55:00Z` Root cause was the custom `input={<OutlinedInput ... />}` prop in `src/components/ui/select.tsx`. In the local Next dev runtime that extra client-element prop was arriving at MUI `Select` malformed enough that MUI crashed while trying to read `input.props.inputProps`. The fix was to stop injecting a custom `OutlinedInput` element there and let the wrapper use MUI's normal outlined-select path (`variant=\"outlined\"`) while keeping the OneSource theme overrides and wrapper API intact.
- `2026-04-22T10:55:00Z` Verification after that fix is green again. Passed: focused local `npm test -- src/components/ui/ui-foundation.test.tsx src/components/opportunities/opportunity-list.test.tsx`; live local-browser repro against `http://127.0.0.1:3000/opportunities` confirming the pipeline heading renders and the error boundary no longer appears; full `make compose-test-lint`; full `make compose-test`; full `make compose-test-build`; full `make compose-test-e2e`; and `git diff --check`. `make compose-test-e2e` tore down the kept live stack as expected, so the default `web`/`worker` stack must be restored again before ending the loop.
- `2026-04-22T10:37:57Z` Completed the broader post-`MUI-14` UI hardening sweep the user requested. The OneSource theme now owns a fuller semantic token set in `src/theme/onesource-theme.ts` (color, typography roles, spacing, radius, elevation, interaction, sizing), the shared wrapper layer (`Surface`, `Button`, `Input`, `Textarea`, `Select`, `Badge`, `DataTable`) now reads those tokens directly instead of relying on Tailwind-era theme classes, and the MUI `CssBaseline` exports the legacy CSS custom properties from the theme so `tailwind-freeze.css` is compatibility-only instead of the active design source.
- `2026-04-22T10:37:57Z` Replaced the app `Select` wrapper with a real MUI `Select` + `MenuItem` implementation while keeping the wrapper API stable for the route code. Two App Router runtime regressions surfaced during browser verification and are now fixed in the worktree: server-rendered routes were passing function-valued `sx` objects into MUI from server components, and the new select wrapper was always creating an inline `onChange` function even when no handler was supplied. I removed the server-side function-valued `sx` usage from the touched routes and wrappers and made `Select` only pass `onChange` when the caller actually provides one.

- `2026-04-21T20:06:55Z` Compose-wide lint, test, and build are green again on the post-timeout-adjustment tree. The first rerun of `make compose-test-e2e` then exposed one real regression and one bounded smoke-runtime issue: `/sources` no longer exposed a visible advanced-filters disclosure because the `<summary>` element had been nested inside `Surface`, and the long opportunity-workspace smoke exceeded Playwright's default `30_000` ms test timeout despite progressing through the workflow and persisting history events successfully. Next step: rerun the required verification chain on this final `MUI-09` tree, including the no-cache browser-image rebuild before `make compose-test-e2e`.
- `2026-04-21T20:30:30Z` Side-step investigation: the main source of verification slowness is that every `docker compose -f docker-compose.test.yml run --rm --build test ...` invocation was building the `runner` target, which always executes `npm run build` before lint, unit tests, Prisma migrate, or seed can even start. I added a dedicated `test` stage to `Dockerfile`, switched the compose `test` service to `target: test`, and added `src/lib/tooling/compose-test-stack.test.ts` so the stack does not drift back to the production `runner` target. A real compose lint invocation confirms the change is active because Docker now logs `test 1/2` and `test 2/2` stages without the old `builder 3/3 RUN npm run build` step. Remaining slowness is still dominated by `docker compose run --rm --build ...` exporting and unpacking a large test image after `COPY . .`; the next optimization, if needed, would be to stop rebuilding on every verification command or move the test service to a bind-mounted source workflow that preserves container-managed dependencies.
- `2026-04-21T20:43:40Z` Implemented the second-layer test optimization for evaluation: `docker-compose.test.yml` now keeps a persistent bind-mounted `test` container alive with a named `/app/node_modules` volume, rehydrates dependency contents from the image when the dependency hash matches, and only falls back to `npm ci` plus `npm run prisma:generate` when dependency inputs change. `Makefile` `compose-test-*` targets now bootstrap that environment once with `compose-test-env-up` and execute lint, unit tests, build, migrate, and seed via `docker compose ... exec -T test ...` instead of `run --rm --build`. Next step: run focused regression coverage, then back-to-back compose timing checks to determine whether the warm-path speedup is worth the persistent-container tradeoff.
- `2026-04-21T20:49:10Z` First cold bootstrap measurement exposed one self-inflicted regression: the new `test` stage was copying `/app/node_modules` twice, once into `/opt/onesource-test/node_modules` for rehydration and again into `/app/node_modules`, even though the bind-mounted service immediately replaces `/app/node_modules` with the named volume. That duplicate image-layer copy made the cold `docker compose -f docker-compose.test.yml up --build -d db test` path much slower than necessary, so I removed the redundant `/app/node_modules` copy and tightened the regression test to assert only the baked rehydration tree under `/opt/onesource-test/node_modules`.
- `2026-04-21T20:52:05Z` The follow-up measurement also confirmed the bigger structural limit: keeping `compose-test-env-up` on `up --build` still forces the expensive image export or unpack path on every compose lint, test, build, migrate, and seed invocation, even with the persistent `test` container. I changed `Makefile` so repeated compose test targets now call `compose-test-env-up` with plain `up -d db test` and added an explicit `compose-test-image` target for opt-in runner rebuilds. Next step: rerun the focused regression coverage, then measure the new cold versus warm path (`compose-test-image`, first `compose-test-lint`, second `compose-test-lint`) to decide whether the workflow tradeoff is worth keeping.
- `2026-04-21T20:54:50Z` Running the persistent-service workflow against the current `TEST_COMPOSE` commands exposed another real integration issue: `docker compose -f docker-compose.test.yml up -d db test` shares the same default project name and `db` service identity as the live stack, so the test bootstrap stalls while colliding with the running development `db` and never creates a `test` container. I isolated the test stack by changing `TEST_COMPOSE` to `docker compose -p onesource-test -f docker-compose.test.yml`, which gives the persistent test DB, test container, and named volumes their own project namespace instead of fighting the live stack.
- `2026-04-21T20:57:40Z` First cold run on the isolated test project proved the image-export fix is working but surfaced a readiness race. `docker compose -p onesource-test -f docker-compose.test.yml up -d db test` completed in about 12 seconds including image export and container creation, but the immediate `exec -T test npm run lint` failed with `sh: 1: eslint: not found` because the `test` container had started before its dependency-hydration command finished copying `/opt/onesource-test/node_modules` into the named volume. I added a `test` service healthcheck for the hydrated marker and `eslint` binary, then changed `compose-test-env-up` to `up -d --wait db test` so follow-on commands only run after the persistent runner is genuinely ready.
- `2026-04-21T21:01:25Z` The long cold wait after adding `--wait` came from a logic bug in the dependency hash comparison, not from the persistent-service approach itself. The compose command was hashing `sha256sum` output that included file paths, so the host-side hash (`package.json`, `prisma/schema.prisma`, etc.) could never equal the image-side hash (`/opt/onesource-test/package.json`, `/opt/onesource-test/prisma/schema.prisma`, etc.), which forced the slow fallback every time. I changed both hashes to use file contents via `cat ... | sha256sum`, so matching dependency inputs now take the intended fast path that copies the baked dependency tree from `/opt/onesource-test/node_modules`.

- `2026-04-19T20:48:36Z` Reproduced the failing Docker `deps`-stage install inside a disposable Linux `node:20-bookworm-slim` container by copying the same package inputs used by the Dockerfile into `/app` and then inspecting `/root/.npm/_logs/*-debug-0.log`. The npm debug log now isolates the real blocker: plain container `npm ci` cannot open direct HTTPS connections to `registry.npmjs.org` and repeatedly fails with `ECONNREFUSED`; npm 10.8.2 then emits `Exit handler never called!` but still returns exit code `0`, leaving a partial `node_modules` tree where `node_modules/prisma` exists but `node_modules/.bin/prisma` does not, which is why the next shell step misleadingly reports `prisma: not found`. Passing explicit proxy env (`HTTP_PROXY` / `HTTPS_PROXY` / lowercase variants set to `http://host.docker.internal:3128`) changes the failure mode to `SELF_SIGNED_CERT_IN_CHAIN`, confirming the runtime expects proxy-mediated egress and the Linux image does not trust the proxy certificate chain. Cleanup is intentionally skipped in this loop so the unresolved container-network debugging evidence remains available.

- `2026-04-19T03:46:52Z` Initial diagnosis from the supplied logs and current code: `/sources` passes `session.user.id` directly into `source_search_executions.requested_by_user_id`, while Auth.js uses JWT-backed sessions that can survive a database reseed. If the `users` row behind the cookie disappears, the page still treats the session as authenticated and Prisma hits the foreign-key failure during `sourceSearchExecution.create()`. The planned fix is to validate JWT sessions against the current `users` table before any authenticated route or action trusts them.
- `2026-04-19T03:52:00Z` Implemented the bounded auth fix in `src/lib/auth/`: JWT-backed sessions now rehydrate their claims from the live `users` table on refresh, clear app-auth fields when the backing user no longer exists or is inactive, and therefore stop stale session cookies from reaching authenticated `/sources` persistence with a dead `requestedByUserId`. Added regression coverage for both the stale-user and refreshed-user cases in `src/lib/auth/auth-options.test.ts`.

- `2026-04-22T15:24:02Z` Started `MUI-15` as a post-`MUI-14` public-surface follow-up after re-reading the durable docs, rechecking `git status`, and reproducing the live `/sign-in` regression in Playwright against the user-kept stack at `http://127.0.0.1:3000`. Acceptance for this loop: fix the shared wrapper contract so caller-provided `sx` arrays survive into MUI, restore the intended width-constrained public shell on `/sign-in` and `/forbidden`, keep sign-in behavior intact, and verify locally without tearing down the user-kept environment.
- `2026-04-22T15:24:02Z` Root cause was shared wrapper composition, not global CSS. `src/components/auth/public-access-shell.tsx` was correctly passing an `sx` array with `maxWidth` and padding into `Surface`, but `src/components/ui/surface.tsx` rewrapped incoming `sx` as `[sx]`; when the caller already passed an array, MUI received a nested array and silently dropped the caller styles. That removed the auth card padding and width constraint in the real browser, stretching `/sign-in` to about `1247px` wide on a `1440px` viewport. The same nested-`sx` pattern also existed in `Input`, `Select`, `Textarea`, `Skeleton`, and `StatePanel`.
- `2026-04-22T15:24:02Z` Implemented the shared fix by adding `src/components/ui/merge-sx.ts` and routing the affected wrappers through it so object and array `sx` inputs flatten correctly instead of nesting. Tightened `PublicAccessShell` spacing and title rhythm while keeping the current visual direction, and moved `SignInForm` to a MUI `Stack component="form"` composition so the page leans more directly on MUI layout primitives without changing Auth.js behavior.
- `2026-04-22T15:24:02Z` Added focused regression coverage in `src/components/ui/merge-sx.test.ts` and `src/components/auth/public-access-shell.test.tsx`. The new shell test asserts that `maxWidth={480}` survives to the rendered section instead of being dropped. Focused local verification was green with `npm test -- src/components/ui/merge-sx.test.ts src/components/auth/public-access-shell.test.tsx src/components/auth/sign-in-form.test.tsx src/components/ui/ui-foundation.test.tsx`.
- `2026-04-22T15:24:02Z` Full verification stayed green after one environment repair. `npm run lint` initially failed because `.docker/postgres-data` had unreadable ownership for host-side ESLint traversal, so a temporary Docker `chown -R 1000:1000 /workspace/.docker` helper restored readability for lint. That in turn broke Postgres access to its bind-mounted data directory for host-side seed, so the loop restored `.docker/postgres-data` to `999:999`, restarted only `db`, and reran `npm run db:seed` successfully before browser verification. Final passing commands: full local `npm run lint`; full local `npm test`; full local `npm run build`; `git diff --check`; `npm run db:seed`; and full local Chromium smoke via `PLAYWRIGHT_BASE_URL=http://127.0.0.1:3002 npm run e2e` against a temporary fixture-backed built server.
